Mr. Telang who does not understand the word **आवार्य** in this sense suggests that**अप्रतिसुखं**should be preferred to **अप्रतिहतम्. अवार्य** may also be taken with **अक्षयनिधिम्** as we have done in translation.

 **SI. 27;** Cf. with this sl. 76. **कण्डुकः** properly means a small round pillow for the check. **दिक्कान्ताभि** &c.—a highly poetical line.**भिक्षू—**

an ascetic, a devotee; and not necessarily a Budhistic mendicant.

 **Sl. 28.तुङ्गा—**

This adds to **च पलव्य भङ्गः—**

Mr. Telang translates this by breaking preferring it to its usual sense of **रचना** but we think the sense of **रच्चना** is more poetic and better as it corresponds to **भोग**the idea of breaking or vanishing being left to be implied. The waves rising in succession **दिनानि—**

the acc by **कालाध्वनोरत्यन्तसंयोगे'** Pàn II 3. 5.**बोधकाः मन्तः** being instructors of people. The word has no special propriety here. It seems to be used here for alliteration. **पेशल—**

may also **चारु** mean beautiful, the **चरुत्व** lying i its excellence**चरौदक्षे च पेशला** Amara **यत्नः** effort may mean an effort to lead people to Moksha; or may Cf refer to the transactions of daily life **यद्यदाचरतिश्रेष्ठस्तत्तदेवेतरो जनः** Bg. III. 21.

 **Sl. 29. वक्यमिक्षते—**

see sl. 66, 92 **प्रत्याशा** hopes, expectations.Here the poet envies the happy lot of the deer. Cf. the idea in Vai S a. sl. 10 fig**अप्रस्तुतप्रशंसा.**

 **Sl. 30.** The same as-Niti S'a sl. 2. with certain variations.

 **S1. 31 जरापरिभव- जराकृतः परिभवः** tho injury or ravages done by old age. Cf. **व्याघ्रीव तिष्टति जराः परिताजयन्ति** supra-sl. 106;.The reading **तदा पुमांसम्**is easier. We need not in this case. supply **पुंस**.. fr: **पुसां** as an object to प**रिहत्यः आरोपित—**

Mt. Telang says that this refers to the bit of bone suspended over a Chândálaku'pa.

 **SI. 32. समारम्भ—**

-attempts well-made; undertakings properly commenced. Cf. Bg. IV. 19 **पशुः—**

because of not becoming wiser by experience. **शतधा न दीर्णम्—**

The many calamities with which worldly life is fraught ought to read the heart.

 **Sl. 33.**This sl. occurs in the Mrcha. **मदयन्ती—**

 i.e.: by their such: blandishments and sportive gestures.**सदयम्** Such a man falls a ready victim to their charms, **वामनयना—**

Mark. the pun is on.वामwhich means (1) beautiful; (2); crooked, destructive.

 Sl. 34. खर—

rough. The moral. is-Magnanimous persons. never. become. slaves of passions.

 **Sl..35. हन्तः—**

a particle expressive of joy. after **हरिन्ये परिचायहः—**

a favorite idea with the poet and referred to in many places.**वृत्ति—**

-Cf. supra sh. 57. **हरभक्तिम्—**

**स्पृहेरीप्सितः.** Pan **ईप्सितामात्रे इयं संज्ञा**। **प्रकर्षविवक्षायां तुः परत्वात्कर्मसंज्ञा॥ पुष्पाणि स्पृहयति।** Sid. Kau. **उपशान्तदेक**whose minds are set on tranquility alone (i.ewho are self-restrained).

 **Sl. 36. स्वादिष्ठ—**

is superlative. Its use with the ablative isunusual Construe**—**

**दैवी वाक् रसंवतः अमृतात्मनः यत् मधुनः घृताच स्वादिष्टं रसवन् असरं प्रसवति तेन &c. दैवी वाक्—**

The Veda, especially the Upanishads which are chiefly concerned with Brahma. No earthly enjoyments give that pleasure to a Yogin which the teaching of the Upanishads do.**आत्मनः** may also be taken separately. The Vedas are eternal. **धृति—**

support, sustenance. There may also here a reference to the divine speech of the poet whose substratum is Rasa sending forth an immortal creation sweeter.than honey &c.

** SL. 37.उन्मीलत्** &c.**उन्मीलन्ती या विन्नली**folds of skin.

above the navel of a woman regarded as A mark of beanty (Cf.Kum I. 39 ), **सेव तरङ्गास्तेषाम् वलयं यस्याः।**

 **उद्यत** &c.**—**

pairs of chakravaka birds are usually described as haunting river-banks. **कुराशाया** has two meanings (1) **कुराः आशयाः वस्याम्**in which there are dangerous aquatic animals; (2) **कुराः आशयाः** thoughts or minds **यस्याः। संसारार्णव—**

Samsdra is the sento which, the river in the form of a woman leads a man.

 **Sl. 38. हतपरमार्थैः—**

ThIndriyas which are often compared to tempt a man further and further away from real bliss.(**मोक्षः**)

SUPPLEMENTARY NOTES.  
ON THE METRES IN THE TWO S'ATAKAS.

 **1** The vowels **अ, ई, उ, ऋ**and स्रुare short and the rest long. The quantity of a syllable is determined by the vowel it ends in. A syllable with a short vowel is called **लघु**or light, and one with a long vowel is called **गुरु** or heavy.

 **2** But if a light syllable is followed by an U*nuswa'ra or Visarga* or by a conjunct consonant the syllable is made heavy. A syllable at the end of a quarter of a sl. may be short or long as the exigency of a metre requires it **सानुस्वारश्च दीर्घश्च विसर्गी च गुरुर्भवेत्। वर्णः संयोगपूर्वश्चः तथा पदन्तगोपि वा॥**

 **3** A short sell. is marked as → and a long one as. The following letters are symbols representing different triads (गणऽ) of light and heavy syllables:—

![](../books_images/U-IMG-1698212860Screenshot2023-10-25111718.png)

 The following couplet will help the student in remembering the long and short syllables forming each Gana **—दिमध्यावसानेषु यरता यान्ति लाघवम्।भजसा गौरवं यान्ति मनौ तु गुरुलाघवम्॥**

 **4** The following are the metres occurring in the two S'atakas:**—**अ**नुष्टुप्, उपजाति, शालिनी, वैतालीय, द्रुतविलंबित, वंशस्थ, वसंततिलका, मालिनी,पृथ्वी, मन्दाक्रान्ता। शिखरिणी, हरिणी, शार्दूलविक्रीडित, स्रग्धरा, आर्या** and **गीति.**

 Their definitions and schemes:**—**

 **अनुष्टुप्ं—**

**अनुष्टुप्** or Sloka is defined as **—**

**पंचमं लघु सर्वत्र सप्तमंद्विचतुर्थयोः। गुरु षष्ठं च पादानां शेषेष्वनियमो मतः॥** In an Anushtup the fifth syll. ought to be short and the sixth long in alt quarters. The seventh should be short in the second and fourth quarters only. Other syllables are governed by no rule.

 **I.** 1, 14, 24, 32, 33, 50, 53, 57, 66, 85, 86, 89, 104, 108. Misc. 8, 13. **II**. 1, 2, 14, 15, 62, 69, 80, Misc. 1. 4, 12, 25.

 **अख्यानकी—**

It is a mixture of Indravajrà and Upendravajrá. See below. I. 7.

 **उपजाति—**

**स्यादिवजा यदि तो जगौगः। उपेद्रवजा जतजास्ततो गौ। अनन्तरो दीरितलक्ष्मभाऔ पादौ यदी यावुपंजातथरताः॥** A mixture of **इन्द्र.** and **उपेन्द्र.** forms **उपजाति** Sch. of G **त त ज ग ग। ज त ज ग ग।**

 **I.** 12, 13, 41, 60, 71, 80, 97, 106. II. 12.

 **शालिनी—**

**भानोगौ वेच्छालेनी वेदलोकैः।**Sch of G. **म त त, ग ग.**

 1. 48. Mis. 5.

 **वैतालीय—**

**षड्विषमेष्टौ समे कलास्ताश्च समे स्युर्निरन्तराः। न समात्र पराश्रिता कला वैतालीयेन्ते रलौ गुरुः॥**The first and third quarters contain six mâtrás (syllabic instants) and the second fourth eight each, followed by a रगणand a short and a long syllable. See also Apte's Dictionary.

 II. 27.

 **द्रुतविलम्बित—**

**द्रुतविलम्बितमाह नभौ भरौ। Sch, न, भ, भ, र०**

 **I.** 52, 63, 91, 92.

** वंशस्थ—**

**जतौ तु वंशस्थमुदीरितं जरो** Sch. **ज, त, ज, र.**

  **I.** 70. Miso. 18. II. 87, 96, Misc. 22.

  **वसन्ततिलका–उक्ता वसन्ततिलका तंभजाजगी गः।** Sch **त, भ, ज, ग. ग.** **I.** 2, 18, 23, 27, 31, 40, 46, 47, 59, 68, 72, 73, 79, 83, 96, 102, 107, 110, II. 19, 67, 70, 72, 73, 74, 106, Misc. 7, 11, 30, 31, 33, 34,,

 मालिनी—

**ननमयययुतेयं मालिनी भोगिलोकैः।** Sch. **न, न, म, य, य. I.** 17, 78, 99 Miso. 22. II. 22, 48, Misc. 17, 38,

 **पृथ्वी—**

**जसौ जसथला वसुग्रहयतिश्च पृथ्वी गुरुः।**  
 Sch. **ज, स, ज, स, ग्र, ल, ग.**  
 **I.** 4, 5, 56, 76. **II.**Misc, 20,

 मन्दाक्रान्ता—

**मन्दाक्रान्ता जलाभिषडमैम्मौ नतो तारू चेत्॥** Sali. **म भ ग,ल, त, ग, ग.**

 1. 58. Misc. 10. II. 38, 40,44, 45, 59, 63, Misc. 27.

 शिखरिणी—

रसैरुद्रैश्छिन्ना

**यमनसभलाः गः शिखरिणी।** Sch. **य, म. न. स, भ..ल, ग.**

 1. 8, 10, 28, 36, 44, 45, 64, 65, 81, 94, Misc. &, 4. 19. II. 6; 9,16, 17, 18, 20, 21, 25, 28, 29, 31, 33, 35, 37. 39, 41, 42, 47, 49, 51, 55, 64, 68, 76, 81, 89, 108, 109 Misc, 2, 8, 10, 18, 23, 32, 35.

  हरिणी—

**नस मरसलागः षड्वेदैर्हयैर्हारिणी मता।** Sch. **न, स, म, रु, स. ल, ग.** 1. 9, 35; Misc. 20. II. 23, 60, 95, Misc. 3.

** शार्दूलविक्रीडित—सूर्या धैर्येदि मः सौ सततगाः शार्दूलविक्रीडितम्।**Soh. **म स ज, स, त, त, ग.**

 **I.** 6, 11, 15, 16, 19, 20, 21, 22, 25, 29, 30; 34, 89, 42, 49, 51, 54, 55, 62, 67, 74, 75, 77, 82, 84, 88, 90, 93, 95, 98, 101, 103,. 109, Mis. I, 7, 9, 11, 15, 16, 23. II. 3. 4, 5, 7, 8, 10, 11, 13, 24, 26,. 32, 34, 36, 43, 46, 52, 54, 56, 57, 58, 61, 65, 75, 77, 78, 82, 83, 84, 85, 86, 88, 91, 93, 94, 97, 98, 99, 100, 101, 102, 101 105. 107, Misc. 5, 6, 9, 13, 14, 15, 16, 17, 21, 26, 28, 29, 36, 37.

 स्रग्धरा—

म्रभ्नैर्यानां

**त्रयेण त्रिमुनियतियुता स्रग्धराकीर्तितेयम्।** Sch **म, र, भ न, य, य, य**.

 **I.** 26, 69,100. II. 30, 50, 53, 66, 71, 79, 90, 92, 108, Mise. 24.

 **आर्या—**

This belongs to the class of metres regulated by the number of mantras or syllabic instants.

यस्याः पादे प्रथमे द्वादश मात्रास्तथा तृतीयेपि।  
अष्टादश द्वितीये चतुर्थके पञ्चादश सार्या॥

** I.** 3, 37, 38, 43, 61, 105. Mis. 1, 6, 12, 14. 17, 21,

** गीति–आर्या प्रथमार्धसमं यस्याः परार्धमीरिता गतिः।**That is Gitt whose. third and fourth quarters are like first and second quarters of an äryd; i. e. whose first and third quarters contain. 12 màtrás and second and fourth 18 matras.

1\. 17.
